<div id="review_2218781927" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2218781927" />
    <a title="Deborah Obida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida"><img alt="Deborah Obida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604679377p2/54790180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2218781927?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Obida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Obida" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida">Deborah Obida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780230758469" href="/book/show/20516386-valour">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2218781927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4316585796315146850"><i>This review is spoiler free for book two, since its almost impossible for me to review this without mentioning the first book, they are tid bits of spoilers from book one, I mentioned names of characters that lived and died so don’t worry about that.</i><br/><br/>This started just where Malice left off, no time jump. This consist of a lot of battle scenes that was so well depicted, why am I even surprise, the book is titled Valour for a reason. Lots of battle means the loss of characters, so many died and oth</span>
  <span id="freeText4316585796315146850" style="display:none"><i>This review is spoiler free for book two, since its almost impossible for me to review this without mentioning the first book, they are tid bits of spoilers from book one, I mentioned names of characters that lived and died so don’t worry about that.</i><br /><br />This started just where Malice left off, no time jump. This consist of a lot of battle scenes that was so well depicted, why am I even surprise, the book is titled Valour for a reason. Lots of battle means the loss of characters, so many died and others are stuck in a situation that is slightly better than dying. The friendship, loyalty, family relationship is what I love most about this book, the way those that made it out of Dun Carreg look out for each, their unusual band that consist of men, women, wolven, birds its funny and I love it. Sadly I didn’t get my wish, people I want dead still lives, more evidence of mean fantasy author. <br /><br />The angels and demons finally made an appearance, I thought the author would drag that to the last book but no he did not, and that battle was epic, angels with wings, that is even cooler than dragons. Another thing that I love about this book is the abundance of great characters, amazing POVs, even the ones I want dead. The author also revealed the dark sun and the bright star and my guesses were correct.<br /><br /><u>World building and Writing</u><br />From the first book we were made aware that the book will have lots of different locations, but more were added here, we get to visit Cambren, Domhain, The Vin Thallum’s island and a host of other which the author did not falter in portraying. The depiction is perfect. The book is written in third person multiple POVs of the characters from the first and some new additional ones like Uthas, Tukul, Fidele, Maquin, Coralen and a host of others.<br /><br /><u>Characters</u><br />The author performed a miracle here cause I was rarely annoyed by any of the characters. Veradis annoyed me a bit but that changed when he voiced out his opinion to Nathair instead of blind followership, I feel so bad for Nathair, whatever will he do now. I hope Veradis don’t abandon him in this cause he trust and love him like crazy.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>There is more chance of my mother assassinating me than of Veradis turning against me. Please – outside.’</i>
</b><br /><br />Corban is still as amazing as ever, he made some decisions that I didn’t agree with but the outcome was worth it, cause if he would have followed blindly they wouldn’t have achieved half of what they did, I hope his loyalty to his friends and family don’t stand in the way of duty cause I doubt things will go this well next time.<br /><br />Cywen my girl, I love this crazy impulsive girl, She really made good decisions here, even the suicidal ones, her bravery is so admirable.<br /><br />Coralen is one of the new characters, if you think Cywen is crazy and badass then you haven’t met this girl, she is arrogant which I hope tunes down in the next book.<br /><br />Maquin just refused to be a pushover, I can already see the danger he will be in the next book, I weep for his enemies, am so glad he is among the good guys.<br /><br />Camlin is just the guy to have around when you are running, he is an amazing scout and his skills with bow and arrow is enviable, glad he switched sides.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>This honour thing, Camlin thought. It has its downside. I’d not think twice about running away. He looked at Edana. Or maybe I would.</i>
</b><br /><br />Now that I know Alycon better, I actually feel bad for him, I loathe Calidus and all this revelations about him.<br /><br />I love Dath and Farrell so much, their conversation is just so hilarious, especially this one.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>‘You’ll need to get yourself a pet wolven,’ Farrell said to Dath.<br />She’s not a pet, thought Corban.<br />‘Like that’s going to happen. How about a crow?’ Dath said. ‘Brina – can I borrow Craf for a while?’<br />‘Ha,’ said Brina, who was sitting a little further along the table. ‘We all know Craf scares you witless.’ <br />‘He does not,’ Dath said.<br />Farrell squawked in Dath’s ear and he jumped, then scowled.<br />‘There’s still hope for us, Dath. Not all of the lasses smile at Corban, anyway,’ Farrell said. ‘Coralen doesn’t.’<br />‘Now, I am scared of her. I think she actually tried to kill you in the practice court today, Ban,’ Dath said.</i>
</b><br /><br />Finally Gwenith and Gar, so glad Corban has them, I love Halion, Marrock, even Vonn, I actually feel bad for him.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4316585796315146850" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1873378874" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1873378874" />
    <a title="Celeste" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste"><img alt="Celeste" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481055226p2/7317186.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1873378874?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celeste" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celeste" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste">Celeste</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330545761" href="/book/show/23248251-valour">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1873378874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14115488909929849087"><b>Full review now posted! Original review can be found on <a href='http://booknest.eu' rel='nofollow noopener'>Booknest</a>.</b><br/><br/><blockquote>“Two born of blood, dust and ashes shall champion the Choices,<br/>the Darkness and the Light.”</blockquote><br/>Valor (or Valour, depending on which copy you end up with) is book two of The Faithful and the Fallen and sequel to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15750692.Malice__The_Faithful_and_the_Fallen___1_' title='Malice (The Faithful and the Fallen, #1) by John Gwynne' rel='nofollow noopener'>Malice</a>. While I thought that Malice was an absolutely incredible debut, <u>Valor did nothing but improve upon an already fantastic story.</u> There have been many comparisons between this series and Martin’s <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13496.A_Game_of_Thrones__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire___1_' title='A Game of Thrones (A Song of Ice and Fire, #1) by George R.R. Martin' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Game of Thrones</a>A Game of T</span>
  <span id="freeText14115488909929849087" style="display:none"><b>Full review now posted! Original review can be found on <a href="http://booknest.eu" rel="nofollow noopener">Booknest</a>.</b><br /><br /><blockquote>“Two born of blood, dust and ashes shall champion the Choices,<br />the Darkness and the Light.”</blockquote><br />Valor (or Valour, depending on which copy you end up with) is book two of The Faithful and the Fallen and sequel to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15750692.Malice__The_Faithful_and_the_Fallen___1_" title="Malice (The Faithful and the Fallen, #1) by John Gwynne" rel="nofollow noopener">Malice</a>. While I thought that Malice was an absolutely incredible debut, <u>Valor did nothing but improve upon an already fantastic story.</u> There have been many comparisons between this series and Martin’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13496.A_Game_of_Thrones__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire___1_" title="A Game of Thrones (A Song of Ice and Fire, #1) by George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">A Game of Thrones</a>A Game of Thrones, and I completely see where these comparisons come from. <b>But The Faithful and the Fallen seems like a much more hopeful and emotionally compelling story than A Song of Ice and Fire, and <u>I believe that one day it will rise above these comparisons and stand firmly on its own as a classic of the genre</u></b>.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Everything I loved about Malice was improved upon in Valor.</i>
</b> The relationships, be they between friends or family or humans and their animals, were handled with finesse, and their growth was completely believable. <b>I have never in my life been so attached to literary animals</b>, and they are many and prevalent in this book. I’m especially attached to Fech, though I love them all. <u>There is a sense of camaraderie in this series that is completely unique.</u> There isn’t the sass present in the Gentleman Bastards series or in Sanderson’s books, but <b>there is a deep closeness between family and friend both human and animal that I’ve never experienced in any other fantasy series.</b> <br /><br /><blockquote>“This world may be full of greed and tragedy and darkness, but I am fortunate beyond measure to have such people around me.”</blockquote><br />And yet, in spite of this closeness, <b>no one is safe. People die. <u>Often.</u></b> And because their attachments to their groups are so emphasized, their loss is felt more keenly than in many other books I’ve read. <u>Every death is mourned</u>, both by the characters left behind and by myself as a reader. <i>(Because of the unavoidable death, I’ve decided not to mention any characters by name. Except Fech. I couldn’t help myself there.)</i><br /><br /><blockquote>“Memory is a double-edged sword. It can keep you strong through dark times, but it can also cripple you, keep you locked in a moment that no longer exists.”</blockquote><br /><b>Something else I really love about this series is the overarching religious and supernatural elements of the war being waged.</b> <u>Spiritual warfare has always fascinated me</u>, and some of my favorite books are Christian fantasies where spiritual warfare is the focus. Gwynne has handled this aspect of his series incredibly well. <b>There is no preachiness here.</b> The spiritual part of the war is presented as matter-of-factly as the rest of the war. And in no way does Gwynne seem to be expressing his own views on religion through his work. <u>It was lovingly and respectfully handled without any aim to proselytize or tear down the beliefs of others, and I appreciate this immensely.</u><br /><br />On to the warfare itself. War has erupted across the land, the smaller pockets we saw in the first book spreading far and wide. And <b>the descriptions of the battles never bored me. Which is one of the biggest compliments I can pay this book.</b> No matter how well written, I almost always get bogged down in books where warfare and battles are such a large part of the narrative. Not so with this series. <u>Gwynne’s descriptions of the battles taking place were completely enthralling.</u> The combat always felt close and personal, even in the presence of new, less than honorable techniques. <br /><br /><b>The world itself also feels close and personal.</b> With Westeros and the lands beyond it in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12177850.A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire__A_Song_of_Ice_and_Fire___1_5_" title="A Song of Ice and Fire (A Song of Ice and Fire, #1-5) by George R.R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">A Song of Ice and Fire</a>, I often felt lost. <u>I never feel lost here in the Banished Lands.</u> They feel tighter, if that makes sense. I never forget where I am. At least, I never forget where I am in the book. Because I often forgot where I physically was while reading. <b>
  <u>This series is absorbing and moving and incredibly well-written, so while I am only halfway through, I have absolutely no qualms about recommending it to any and everyone.</u>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="14115488909929849087" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2053195354" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2053195354" />
    <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries"><img alt="Mayim de Vries" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560508357p2/50424456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2053195354?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mayim de Vries" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries">Mayim de Vries</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316399746" href="/book/show/18513718-valor">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2053195354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11347365124860128124">When I started reading Valour, the most common reaction was: <i>“I thought you hated Malice!”</i><br/><br/>I am not sure “hated” is the best word to describe my relationship with Malice (check for yourself), but it is what it is mainly because I expected a masterpiece. Since my expectations suffered and then died a slow and painful way during the previous instalment, <b>reading Valour was OK because I knew I will get a mediocre book</b>.<br/><br/><i>“Aha! So you still have ISSUES!”</i> you want to exclaim (please, do it for me and pron</span>
  <span id="freeText11347365124860128124" style="display:none">When I started reading Valour, the most common reaction was: <i>“I thought you hated Malice!”</i><br /><br />I am not sure “hated” is the best word to describe my relationship with Malice (check for yourself), but it is what it is mainly because I expected a masterpiece. Since my expectations suffered and then died a slow and painful way during the previous instalment, <b>reading Valour was OK because I knew I will get a mediocre book</b>.<br /><br /><i>“Aha! So you still have ISSUES!”</i> you want to exclaim (please, do it for me and pronounce it like Helena Bonham Carter in “King’s Speech”). Indeed, issues I have with this book that among my friends reaped 5-star reviews (with one single exception of 4 *gasp!*), and all continue the old ailments of the first book in the series. <br /><br /><b>The problem of special snowflake(s) intensifies.</b> We are told now and again how special, different and chosen Corban and Nathair are. The avatars of the divine, the unique ones, <b>they really made me vomit with wonder. And the main problem is not the fact that both of these young men are these things, but that if not for the repeated refrain, the reader would not have guessed this being the case.</b> <i>Ah!</i>, you want to interject, <i>but Corban has, you know, the dreams (he, mostly, does not remember, let me add acerbically) and the encounters with, you know, the spiritual, the otherworldly!</i> That he has, they both do. But this thing only underlines my point here: <b>he is special not by the virtue of his deeds but because of what happens to him and of which he is either unconscious or unwilling participant. The same applies to his dark counterpart</b>. <br /><br />To be fair, this shortcoming is not limited to the main protagonists. Take Edana. At the beginning we read that Edana is so traumatised by what has happened with her parents and hear realm that she is (and I quote) <i>“not fit to lead the pony”</i>. Later on, she recovers somewhat, but does not develop a personality, cunning, charisma or courage. Throughout the book, she is either led by the other characters or swept by tide of events. The moments when she is given agency that tips the scales or is truly extraordinary are next to none. And yet, at the end we are told that she has (and I quote) <i>“a wise head on her shoulders”.</i> Where is a proof of that? Where can we see a character development similar to that shown by Joe Abercrombie in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1985190589" rel="nofollow noopener">Half a War</a> with regard to princess Skara? (Hint, hint: nowhere!)<br /><br />My conclusion is that Mr Gwynne either simply likes telling or that he thinks he is not doing that because all makes perfect sense in his head. Sadly, <b>the reader can deuce how things are not by reading Mr Gwynne’s mind but reading the pages of the book. And what is on those does not speak for itself</b>, instead needs the verbal reinforcement that is not credible at all. <br /><br />My favourite example is the whole Cywen-related plot. It is so preposterous that I decided fuming with indignation is pointless and instead I read those chapters like a comic relief. The way she behaves, the way she is treated by Nathair and Veradis (in truth the only person who treats her appropriately to the brattiness she espouses is Calidus, oh how I rooted for you old man!), the way she is rescued. My, the whole grand finale surpassed Monty Python <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[with how come the ragtag group managed to sneak upon the whole might of Black Sun, steal the prised possession and then happily escape <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. I did laugh out loud.<br /><br />This is related to the problematic female protagonists. Cywen is a prime example, but then we are introduced to Coralen and it turns out that Coralen is Cywen by other name. Another girl grotesque in her propensity to hurt or promise to hurt everyone around (especially men and pretty women as if to prove something). Coralen is an insecure, spiteful creature unable to respond without resorting to violence (even if only verbally). <br /><br /><i>“Enjoy your victory,” she said with a sneer and walked away.</i> <br /><br />How cute is that. Wouldn’t you like to be her friend? <br /><br />We do not have a love triangle (yet) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Instead, we have two sets of romantic subplots Veradis-Cywen and Corban-Coralen. Veradis is called the True-Heart in the book, so I assume he will abandon Nathair because in the prophecy it is said that True Heart accompanies one avatar and Black Heart, i.e. Calidus the other. I even hoped that he would do so because of Cywen’s death, sadly she survived. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but meeting Coralen made me think this wouldn’t be such a terrible idea after all. <br /><br />Lines sparking with humour and finesse are still rare. Character development means that Corban’s playing the considerate pacifist in this instalment (as oppose to previous book, where he lived in the land of denial). When something is supposed to happen, it happens regardless of how idiotic the thing objectively is. Lines like (and I quote) <i>“somehow Edana had talked her way into coming”</i>, somehow this happened or that took place are a common feature in this story. <br /><br />Still, the book has some valour in it. Not all is bad: <b>I like the way the spiritual is brought about in the book</b>, but still majority of the dilemmas strike me as banal and <b>the main question whether or not every human being has a seed of darkness in their soul and how we fight it or why do we yield is not explored</b>. I like how Mr Gwynne writes about <b>family and friendship</b> even if he ventures to the land of cheesy at times. <b>Maquin is the strongest, most complex character, and undoubtedly my favourite</b>. A true fighter, incredibly well written and alone makes the book worth reading. There are good dying scenes and good dying lines.<br /><br /><i>“I’d rather standard die than see you become the thing we’ve both hated.”</i><br /><br />“Sometimes it is not about the winning, it is about how you lose.” <br /><br />It nearly makes me wish there is more dying around. Maybe in Ruin? <br />__<br /><br /><b>Other reviews:</b><br /><br />Pure <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1773108319?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Malice</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2061343816" rel="nofollow noopener">Ruin</a>-ation <br />Cape <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2072972154" rel="nofollow noopener">Wrath</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11347365124860128124" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Book two is way more different, I loved it from the very start till the very end. Wow, just wow, the adventures, intrigues, fighting, friendships, loves, secrets, betrayals, lots of action and suspense...   <span id="freeText6076259480534637368" style="display:none">After Malice I didn't know what to expect from Mr. Gwynne. <div id="review_3045026802" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3045026802" />
    <a title="ChopinFC" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/51633786-chopinfc"><img alt="ChopinFC" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545283749p2/51633786.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3045026802?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ChopinFC" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ChopinFC" href="/user/show/51633786-chopinfc">ChopinFC</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51633786-chopinfc?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51633786-chopinfc?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/51633786-chopinfc?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3045026802" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6430251745031995460"><b>5 Stars (Phenomenal)</b><br/><br/>You known the feeling when you're reading a book that is so good, that you immerse yourself completely into the story and you never want it to end? <br/><br/> <b><i>Valor</i> is that incredible of a book!!</b><br/><br/>John Gwynne has catapulted from a very good fantasy writer, to my top 5 fantasy authors just like that! The writing, the prose, the characters are so well written- that at times I slowed myself deliberately to make the story last a little longer, hehe. <br/><br/>We pick up the action immediately after th</span>
  <span id="freeText6430251745031995460" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars (Phenomenal)</b><br><br>You known the feeling when you're reading a book that is so good, that you immerse yourself completely into the story and you never want it to end? <br><br> <b><i>Valor</i> is that incredible of a book!!</b><br><br>John Gwynne has catapulted from a very good fantasy writer, to my top 5 fantasy authors just like that! The writing, the prose, the characters are so well written- that at times I slowed myself deliberately to make the story last a little longer, hehe. <br><br>We pick up the action immediately after the events of 'Malice', where kingdoms are in complete disarray, and multiple betrayals and wars have ensued amongst the banished land. The end result is a dissonant and grim environment where death and savagery are the driving forces. There's a clear delineation of good vs. evil, as Corban surfaces as the chosen 'Bright Star' to fight the evil champion of 'Asroth' the nefarious God. <br><br><b>The plot and characterization are even better than the first book!</b> We see fostered relationships grow stronger, and love or hatred between characters rise and fall in a dynamic interplay. Corban's sister, 'Cywen', has been 'taken' by the evil forces of Asroth- and we see an incredible journey of rescue take place. It was so cool, as <i>Valor</i> reads much like 'The Two Towers'(Lord of the Rings), where Aragorn and his band go after the 2 hobbies kidnapped! Corban and his band are so well developed- that each character ( whether human of animal) adds to the cohesiveness of the group. <br><br>Gwynne is very adept at writing animals into the story. Corban's wolf 'Storm' and eventually his immaculate horse are incredibly important to the sense of 'family' and trustworthiness. Even a a talking crow and a raven play a key role into the narrative, and add much fun and aid to Corban's group! In essence the 2 bands that develop are marred by hatred and mistrust or trust and friendship.<br><br> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1490192111i/22289768._SY540_.jpg" width="350" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>Corban and his wolven Snow<br><br><br> “This world may be full of greed and tragedy and darkness, but I am fortunate beyond measure to have such people about me.”<br>― John Gwynne, Valour <br><br><br>“You can tell much about a man by the company he keeps, by his friends, and his enemies,”<br>― John Gwynne, Malice</i><br><br><b>The action scenes are vast and organically placed in the story- adding much to the grandness of this tale.</b> Gwynne writes the shit out of action scenes, and 'the calm before the storm' could not be more overly stated in his narrative. One moment everything is quiet, and a band of soldiers/people are in the forest traveling peacefully.... next <u>all shit hits the fan</u>, and arrows are flying, Giants appear swinging massive hammers, wolves come attacking and sword fights are intricately plotted! <br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1576537599i/28623687._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>the storm after the calm</i><br><br><br><b> Overall <i>Valor</i> has catapulted into my 'favorite' of all time list, with incredible storytelling, characterization and action. Ultimately is the emotional bond we form for recurring characters that leads me so pschyed about continuing this journey!<br><br>5 Stars!!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="6430251745031995460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1981920552" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1981920552" />
    <a title="Liam Degnan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8180038-liam-degnan"><img alt="Liam Degnan" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1981920552?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liam Degnan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liam Degnan" href="/user/show/8180038-liam-degnan">Liam Degnan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316399746" href="/book/show/18513718-valor">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Your family, your friends, your cousin Rick, your aunt Ethel - EVERYBODY.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8180038-liam-degnan?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8180038-liam-degnan?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1981920552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5751340069478884595"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Memory is a double-edged sword, Uthas. It can keep you strong through dark times, but it can also cripple you, keep you locked in a moment that no longer exists.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/><br/><b>
  <u>A Full Five Stars: ✰✰✰✰✰</u>
</b><br/><br/>Absolutely <b>riveting</b> continuation of a series that is as gripping as it is brutal. A slow start that turned into nothing other than a perfect sequel. I was blown away by how good it was. From the themes, the story, the characters - even the action and battle scenes - John Gwynne shows himself to b</span>
  <span id="freeText5751340069478884595" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Memory is a double-edged sword, Uthas. It can keep you strong through dark times, but it can also cripple you, keep you locked in a moment that no longer exists.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>A Full Five Stars: ✰✰✰✰✰</u>
</b><br /><br />Absolutely <b>riveting</b> continuation of a series that is as gripping as it is brutal. A slow start that turned into nothing other than a perfect sequel. I was blown away by how good it was. From the themes, the story, the characters - even the action and battle scenes - John Gwynne shows himself to be a truly great writer, and if this trend continues he is sure to be listed among my favorite authors of all time. I'm going to break this down into just a few of my favorite elements from this book in particular, because this book really is truly unique compared to what's currently out there in terms of fantasy. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Life was so frail, and he had not just seen men die, an impartial observer, he had taken lives himself. More than I can remember. . . What am I becoming?” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Themes:</u>
</b><br /><br />By far my favorite thing about the way that John Gwynne writes are the themes that he weaves into these stories. In the first book, the biggest theme communicated was all about fear. In this book, as each of our characters more forwards in their place in this story, we see them dealing with the harsh reality of <b>becoming somebody that they don't want to be</b> in the face of suffering, war, and loss. Even from the villain's point of view, we see how easy it is to be deceived by the simple belief that what you are doing is right, and how this kind of self-deception can lead you down path you never thought you would be walking down. <br /><br />So many books have too many happy endings, with heroes who are unwavering in their pursuit of what is good and right - and there is a place for those books. I'm not saying we shouldn't have stories with idealized heroes. What makes this book so refreshing is how <b>totally different</b> it is in that our heroes have to fight through pain, loss, grief, and a lot of blood as they strive to reach their goals. We see them dealing with painful realities of life, doing things they wish they didn't have to do, often paralyzed by their regrets, and it is heart wrenching. <b>This series has a realness to it that I've never experienced before in a book</b>, and each POV contributes to this in an excellent way. A lot of books try to accomplish this through brutal, violent content - in a gratuitous way, while this book actually accomplishes it mostly through the characters and themes Gwynne writes about. And while this book definitely has it's share of brutality, it is never without reason, and it wasn't offensive or overly graphic like many Grimdark novels can be. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Is the human heart so fickle? So ready to embrace such evil?”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Action:</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>The fights and battles scenes in this series are some of the best I have ever read</b>. This applies on a large scale, and on a small scale. Somehow Gwynne can write about a battle with thousands of men on either side, while still having the fights between just two people be equally captivating. Maquin's POV in this book, though it started off slow, turned into one of my favorites if only because of the incredible fight sequences that he goes through. I can't really speak highly enough about this aspect of the series - just read it. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Without fear there is no courage.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Characters:</u>
</b><br /><br />If for no other reason, Gwynne's talent as an author is shown through his ability to write dozens of characters, with a huge amount of POVs sprinkled throughout, and still make each of them interesting and compelling. <br /><br />I've never seen a cast of characters quite like what we have in this book. Gwynne gives us POVs and perspectives on characters that are obviously good, and characters that are obviously bad (that's a given). But he also writes characters that are <b>becoming</b> good and doing their best to redeem themselves from their past. In addition to this, <b>most interestingly, he writes from the perspective of characters who start out as heroes and slowly become villains without realizing it</b>. And it is actually believable. It's unlike anything I've read before. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>In Conclusion:</u>
</b><br /><br />My "favorite series" list is very small, even though my favorites books list is large, because a series really needs to blow me away if I'm going to call it a favorite as a whole. If the last two books of this series are as good as the first two, <b>then it's safe to say that this will be tied with Mistborn as my second favorite series of all time</b>. Just under Stormlight. It is that good. <br /><br />Can't recommend it enough. <br /><br />For this review and more, check out my blog: <a href="https://thoughtsofathousandlives.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Thoughts of a Thousand Lives</a>. <br /><br />Happy reading =].</span>
  <a data-text-id="5751340069478884595" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1939383140" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1939383140" />
    <a title="Lema" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18145934-lema"><img alt="Lema" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1507843225p2/18145934.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1939383140?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lema" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lema" href="/user/show/18145934-lema">Lema</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780230758469" href="/book/show/20516386-valour">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Lema by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18145934-lema?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18145934-lema?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1939383140" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8950508402204824232"><b>I have officially crossed over from the Dark Side...I am a HARDCORE FAN as of now!<br/>This book you guys! this glorious wonderful brutal heart-wrenching book!!</b><br/><br/>I literally went from this during Malice (Click <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1816013668' rel='nofollow noopener'>here</a> for my not-so-happy review)..<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1408112150ra/10808389.gif' width='381' height='178' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/>..to THIS, and only from reading two chapters of Valour..<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421813029ra/13419114.gif' width='381' height='225' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>It's like everything I didn't like about Malice has just vanished and everything I DID like has been expanded on like there's no tomorrow.. I just loved Valour to pieces, and the series has finally taken </span>
  <span id="freeText8950508402204824232" style="display:none"><b>I have officially crossed over from the Dark Side...I am a HARDCORE FAN as of now!<br>This book you guys! this glorious wonderful brutal heart-wrenching book!!</b><br><br>I literally went from this during Malice (Click <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1816013668" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a> for my not-so-happy review)..<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1408112150ra/10808389.gif" width="381" height="178" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br>..to THIS, and only from reading two chapters of Valour..<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1421813029ra/13419114.gif" width="381" height="225" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>It's like everything I didn't like about Malice has just vanished and everything I DID like has been expanded on like there's no tomorrow.. I just loved Valour to pieces, and the series has finally taken its place in my heart as one of the best I've read in fantasy despite our rocky beginnings!<br><br><b>The plot really doesn't allow you to breathe</b>, everything becomes intricate and convoluted but in a very fluid way.. When POV changes between chapters, it isn't clunky anymore and it is done in a way that gives you a full immersive experience. Sub-plots are sprouting everywhere but they are all pertinent to the bigger picture, and I care about EVERY. SINGLE. ONE. OF. THEM! it's not about training the young warriors and attacking some random giant camps anymore, it became much MUCH MORE than that, a ragtag band of refugees running for their lives, hot pursuits, badass animals, brutal sieges, moral crises, slavery, pit fighting... and that's just the first third of the book :'D<br><br><b>The Characters are EVERYTHING! now that's a dramatic 180 turn if I've ever seen one..</b><br>I had major trouble imagining them in Malice, and whenever I managed to picture them in a certain way, something happens and makes that picture crumble away, or they just turn out to be passing by never to be seen again, which was a source of endless frustration for me.<br>However, now that I identified the major players and knew exactly about their deeds and where their loyalties lie everything came to me much easier and I was able to appreciate more their varied personalities and discern their indeed unique voices.<br>I also commented about lack of variety since all the recurring characters in Malice are teenage boys training to be warriors, <b>well Valour couldn't surprise me better than with a cast of badass ladies in all shapes and sizes!</b> <br><b>Cywen</b> -which was my favorite character in Malice and continues to be my fave in Valour- has finally spread her own wings and is no longer used as a device to drive Corban's narrative, she's the heroine of her own storyline and she's freaking SLAYING IT!<br>Not to mention that my shipping heart has also started to beat full force... Nothing cripples your interactions with regular humans like a book throwing in your face all these wonderful possibilities for happiness and then pulling the rug from under your feet :')<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1482962459ra/21566852.gif" width="400" height="198" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Seriously, this book gave me all the feels..literally! I laughed and snickered at the banter between them (Brina again, that old lady is gold!), I cried buckets of tears at the emotional parts, I felt hot red anger (I wish I could run into <b>Lykos</b>..preferably with a kitchen knife) and I felt deep fear for my favorite characters because everyone is prone to endless suffering <s>me included</s>.<br><br>Finally, I just wanna recommend reading this with your buddies because you'll need your circle of emotional support (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1785617448%20" rel="nofollow noopener">Petrik</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1875497527%20" rel="nofollow noopener">Haïfa</a> you guys are the best!)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1489674439ra/22238793.gif" width="500" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Why do I feel I'll be using this gif a lot in the coming days? :')<br>*runs to read Ruin*</span>
  <a data-text-id="8950508402204824232" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

"Valor" outshone its predecessor and gets an unreserved five-star rating. <br/><br/>This is the book that kept me up late, the one that took my attention away from my family, the one that made me wonder what the characters were doing when I was away from them.<br/><br/>Mr. Gwynne has made me know these people, invest in them and their world, feel their pain and share their triumphs.   <span id="freeText11078964746255608361" style="display:none">I had given "Malice" a very solid four stars. "Valor" outshone its predecessor and gets an unreserved five-star rating. <br /><br />This is the book that kept me up late, the one that took my attention away from my family, the one that made me wonder what the characters were doing when I was away from them.<br /><br />Mr. Gwynne has made me know these people, invest in them and their world, feel their pain and share their triumphs. The last few pages had my mouth gaping open.<br /><br />I don't need to say much more. There are plenty of synoptic reviews out there. The book is amazing. Get them. Read them. Now. Thank god I have "Ruin" already in my hands. <br /><br />Kudos, Mr. Gwynne!</span>

<div id="review_1296181381" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1296181381" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1296181381?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330545761" href="/book/show/23248251-valour">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19126246-kaitlin?shelf=my-sff-faves">my-sff-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1296181381" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11141004606392597475">This book is the second one in this series and after enjoying the first one a lot and giving it an easy 4* rating I was hoping for things to improve and become more exciting as the series went on; that certainly did seem to be the case! This story continues immediately after the ending of the first which is wonderful because it meant that we could get back into the action and story straight away. The characters that we know and enjoyed in the first book are back, and we also have a fair few new </span>
  <span id="freeText11141004606392597475" style="display:none">This book is the second one in this series and after enjoying the first one a lot and giving it an easy 4* rating I was hoping for things to improve and become more exciting as the series went on; that certainly did seem to be the case! This story continues immediately after the ending of the first which is wonderful because it meant that we could get back into the action and story straight away. The characters that we know and enjoyed in the first book are back, and we also have a fair few new povs which really helps to enhance the story and make it very immersive.<br /><br />This story focuses largely on a great war between men and gods. There was once a prophecy that talked about two people being born and casting chaos onto the land. One would be the Black Sun, Asroth's chosen and the leader of the Fallen. The other would be the Bright Star, Elyon's chosen and the leader of the Faithful. These people are unknown by most, but at this point of the story it seems that we (the reader) might be able to understand who is who and tyr to guess at what will happen when they clash.<br /><br />The thing I most enjoyed about this book is that the chapters are all very short and snappy which means that you're constantly being told new information, following the development of a character or scheme, or you're being shown some action. The flow of the book was easy to get through and fun to follow and I have to say that the pacing was well done. <br /><br />The characters of this world range from humans to wolves to giants to gods. There are all sorts of alliances and enemies from each race and everyone has to choose which side they will fight for, the Black Sun or the Bright Star (a hard choice when not everyone knows who is who).<br /><br />The characters worth noting include:<br /><br />- Corban - a young boy who is the central focus of a lot of this story but who doesn't really now why. Corban has been through a fair amount of struggles and loss in his young life and he's dealt well with what he's been given. He's a fighter and he's very loyal to those he is friends with, he's a character who knows that he needs to stick with his friends and rely on them to make it through the chaos that is engulfing their world.<br /><br />- Maquin - a member of the Gadrai who is set on a path of vengeance through the events of this book. He too knows the value of his Shield-Brothers and fights valiantly alongside them through various battles and confrontations. He's a resilient type and when things do not always go his way he still sticks true to his path and does his best to face whatever is thrown at him.<br />His storyline took some interesting turns that I didn't expect and very much enjoyed.<br /><br />- Nathair - the Young King who is leading his followers on a rather large undertaking. He believes in a noble cause and he will do anything to achieve his final goals because he feels that what he is doing is right. He is a good leader and a fair one, but that doesn't mean he always does the best things. He is still young and with all sorts of enemies and outside influences trying to sway him from his cause and push him to theirs he faces many struggles.<br /><br />- Veradis - the First-Sword and friend of Nathair he is one of the originals from Nathair's war-band. He's a brilliant fighter who trains day in day out and comes up with some new and useful ideas for the field of battle. He's loyal to a fault and will never abandon his leader, but when doubts begin to plague him and he's unsure of the true purpose he faces some internal strife and hard questions.<br /><br />- Rhin - is a Queen who is trying to take over a lot of the Banished Lands (the world this is set in) with a large force. She believes that she should rule all of the West and she is ruthless and ready to take whatever is not freely handed to her. She's nasty and cruel, but also very clever which makes her a character to look out for and not one you'd wish to cross.<br /><br />- Fidele - is the mother of Nathair and the Regent in his time away leading his war-band on their quest. She is a fair and just leader who is trying to do the best thing for her people and when the safety of her land is questioned by the Vin Thalen (an ally) she's forced to take some more drastic actions. I liked her sections, although small, for the interesting perspective she gave and the look into the land where she was and how it changed over the course of this book.<br /><br />- Cywen - is Corban's sister and she plays an important role in this book by being our eyes and ears in one of the different war-camps from her family. She's a character who feels lonely and worried for the fate of her friends and family, and so she strikes out at the people she's with many times over the course of the book. Despite this feistyness she's actually a wonderful character to read about and her thoughts and ideas about the situation she's in and what to do were some of the things I enjoyed most about her.<br /><br />One other interesting thing to note was that the animals of this world and the magic of this world also play a bigger role in this book than the first and I very much enjoyed seeing them take a more prominent part in the story.<br /><br />On the whole I have to say that this book was a lot more action-packed and fun than the first one which was fabulous and I am now very eager for the next and final one in the series to be released (next month) so I can pick it up and find out what happens next. Despite using a fair amount of troupes in the story Gwynne also throws in some great surprises and this makes it a lot of fun trying to guess what may happen. A really well-written and fun read, 5*s </span>
  <a data-text-id="11141004606392597475" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1752065257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11345017733914049425">Valor = Valour (The Faithful and the Fallen, #2), John Gwynne<br/><br/>The second in The Faithful and the Fallen series, Valour by John Gwynne carries all of the excitement of the first.<br/><br/>The Banished Lands are torn by war as the army of High King Nathair sweeps the realm challenging all who oppose his holy crusade. Allied with the manipulative Queen Rhin of Cambren, there are few who can stand against him. But Rhin is playing her own games and has her eyes on a far greater prize . . .<br/><br/>Left for dead – her ki</span>
  <span id="freeText11345017733914049425" style="display:none">Valor = Valour (The Faithful and the Fallen, #2), John Gwynne<br /><br />The second in The Faithful and the Fallen series, Valour by John Gwynne carries all of the excitement of the first.<br /><br />The Banished Lands are torn by war as the army of High King Nathair sweeps the realm challenging all who oppose his holy crusade. Allied with the manipulative Queen Rhin of Cambren, there are few who can stand against him. But Rhin is playing her own games and has her eyes on a far greater prize . . .<br /><br />Left for dead – her kin have fled and her country is overrun with enemies – Cywen fights to survive. But any chance of escape is futile once Nathair and his disquieting advisor Calidus realize who she is. They have no intention of letting such a prize slip from their grasp. For she may be their one chance at killing the biggest threat to their power.<br /><br />Meanwhile, the young warrior Corban flees from his conquered homeland with his exiled companions, heading for the only place that may offer them sanctuary. But to get there they must travel through Cambren, avoiding warbands, giants and the vicious wolven of the mountains. And all the while Corban struggles to become the man that everyone believes him to be – the Bright Star and saviour of the Banished Lands.<br /><br />Embroiled in struggles for power and survival, the mortal world is unaware of the greatest threat of all. In the Otherworld, dark forces scheme to bring a host of the Fallen into the world of flesh to end the war with the Faithful, once and for all.<br /><br />تاریخ خوانش روز هجدهم ماه فوریه سال 2017 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: جسارت: کتاب دوم از سری ایمان و فروافتاده؛ نویسنده: جان گوین؛<br /><br />ا. شربیانی</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1337746677?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jody " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jody " href="/user/show/41767362-jody">Jody </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41767362-jody?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1337746677" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13084876613980964159">I have spent all of my free time reading so much lately that I haven’t put in the time for my reviews that I should. So, with that being said….here we go!<br/><br/>Another amazing novel in the world of The Faithful and the Fallen. Mr. Gwynne has given us another work of art that was fun to read, and hard to put down. The pacing of this book doesn’t let up throughout. It’s full of action and breathtaking battle scenes described with extreme detail and gore. We are introduced to new characters, and say good</span>
  <span id="freeText13084876613980964159" style="display:none">I have spent all of my free time reading so much lately that I haven’t put in the time for my reviews that I should. So, with that being said….here we go!<br /><br />Another amazing novel in the world of The Faithful and the Fallen. Mr. Gwynne has given us another work of art that was fun to read, and hard to put down. The pacing of this book doesn’t let up throughout. It’s full of action and breathtaking battle scenes described with extreme detail and gore. We are introduced to new characters, and say goodbye to others as they cross the bridge of swords. <br /><br />Every turn of the page can bring either heartbreak, rage, hope, or a variety of other emotions that make this an incredible story true to the genre. Whether it be epic fantasy or grimdark. This is the type of fantasy novel I love to read!<br /><br /> 5 Bright Stars *****<br /></span>

<div id="review_1714415912" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1714415912" />
    <a title="Solseit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57608403-solseit"><img alt="Solseit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501748227p2/57608403.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1714415912?book_show_action=true">Jul 31, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Solseit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Solseit" href="/user/show/57608403-solseit">Solseit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/21324349-valour">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1714415912" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6430062404237122216">"They must be stopped".<br/><br/>The easy way to summarize this book is: stunning continuation of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15750692.Malice__The_Faithful_and_the_Fallen___1_' title='Malice (The Faithful and the Fallen, #1) by John Gwynne' rel='nofollow noopener'>Malice</a>. Actually, I even liked this book more, somehow; I believe it is mostly because I already knew all the characters from the first book and this book focused more on the plot and character development.<br/><br/>I just finished the book and I am just speechless <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ I guess the same way Nathair was at the end of the book in realizing what he really is  <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br/><br/>I really loved the book: political i</span>
  <span id="freeText6430062404237122216" style="display:none">"They must be stopped".<br /><br />The easy way to summarize this book is: stunning continuation of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15750692.Malice__The_Faithful_and_the_Fallen___1_" title="Malice (The Faithful and the Fallen, #1) by John Gwynne" rel="nofollow noopener">Malice</a>. Actually, I even liked this book more, somehow; I believe it is mostly because I already knew all the characters from the first book and this book focused more on the plot and character development.<br /><br />I just finished the book and I am just speechless <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I guess the same way Nathair was at the end of the book in realizing what he really is  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />I really loved the book: political intrigue, war, battles, duel, bandits, magic, people with good hearts, evil and people making bad choices. There are so many characters involved in the book and the more time you spend reading the book the more you get to know them <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ and your heart breaks when they die, because yes, John Gwynne kills characters in the book which is the right way to go for this kind of fantasy but it does not make this book less painful when a death occurs. I actually cried when Marrock was killed.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />The plot is just so intricate and clear that is a great piece of art. The way all the threads are pulled and the characters intertwine is just amazing. At this point, I think this is the strongest element of the book. Also, it does not appear there are unnecessary twists or conversations in the book which I really appreciated!<br /><br />The characters are just the right people at the right moment. I did not find any character in this book that was less than what he or she was supposed to be. Obviously I have favorites and disliked but this is a book that needs to lead to that, it is a book with polarized factions and the more the story continues the more people will be on either side of the story. (Side note, it seems this year is the year of opposing forces even at the movies, Batman v Superman, Cap America: Civil War). <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ My favorites by far are Maquin, Camlin, Hadolin and Gar. I guess the common elements are the golden heart, the fighting and their altruism. Or stupidity, depending from where you look at it I guess. <br />In particular, I enjoyed the storyline of Maquin. Not only he has revenge lining up against one of the worst characters of the book, Jael (who incidentally is part of my disliked list), but he also embarks in this almost gladiatory sequence of events and feels like Spartacus, with a very different outcome from what I could tell so far. <br /><br />As for female characters, I also really enjoyed Coralen - finally a woman who is a real fighter and strong and independent and smart and she can make a difference in battle. Yet she has her own demons and she needs to deal with significant events in her own life. <br />Cywen keeps being an all time favorite character, making the best of what the world offers to her. <br />Finally Fidele is a point of view that tackles significant topics, such as slavery and rape and I found the interest of John Gwynne to incorporate these themes in the book on point and they are also properly treated in the book, at least in my opinion. <br /><br />As to the disliked, Jael needs to be obliterated but in a painful way, coward and brown-nose. <br />Calidus is a snake, actually the snake and deserves to be torn apart as brutally as possible. <br />Lykos is a desperate man with an extremely limited regard for human life yet the reason he is on this list is his abuse of a woman in this book and it cannot be tolerated. <br />Rhin for being the vicious little woman she is. She is part of the reason our main characters are grieving and she has no human emotions, besides rage and greed. <br />Finally Evnis primarily because he chose a long time ago to serve the god of darkness and his was a voluntary decision based on jealousy for his own brother.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />The medieval setting - and I hope I am not mistaken in making this statement - is just consistently maintained. I am not expert in medieval history yet it appears that all the elements described in the book are what I would expect in this kind of setting (yes, I do not see any camera man walking in the middle of the screen like in the Gladiator by Ridley Scott, if you remember!).<br />I really enjoy the amount of magic and the consistency of the magic applied. I also felt in love with the talking ravens <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[, especially the grieve they experience. It was a very touching moment for me  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />Did you read it? If you did not start yet, I really encourage you to start with Malice. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27411345.Wrath__The_Faithful_and_the_Fallen___4_" title="Wrath (The Faithful and the Fallen, #4) by John Gwynne" rel="nofollow noopener">Wrath</a>, the fourth and last book of the series, is going to be published in November so you have time enough to be updated!<br /><br />Ah, one more point: I finally found out who Ventos was reporting to and I have to say I was a bit disappointed, I was almost hoping for a more epic participation of Ventos in the events!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6430062404237122216" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1430008324" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1430008324" />
    <a title="Stefan Bach" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24053713-stefan-bach"><img alt="Stefan Bach" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603215087p2/24053713.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1430008324?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stefan Bach" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stefan Bach" href="/user/show/24053713-stefan-bach">Stefan Bach</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780230758469" href="/book/show/20516386-valour">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1430008324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17879433320706899037"><i>
  <b>“Allons enfants de la Patrie,<br/>The day of glory has arrived!<br/>Against us tyranny's<br/>Bloody banner is raised!”</b>
</i><br/><br/>This book is a perfect example why I think rating books with numbers (of stars or pine cones or whatever else you could think of) is needless and futile. <br/>Is <i>Valour</i> the greatest book I have ever read? Hell no.<br/>Is it a good one? Couldn’t say that either.<br/>Then it’s a bad one? No, no, no.<br/>Then what is?<br/>It’s a decent enough book. <br/>And if we’re going to be “strictly technical” <i>Valour’s</i> worth is of two</span>
  <span id="freeText17879433320706899037" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“Allons enfants de la Patrie,<br />The day of glory has arrived!<br />Against us tyranny's<br />Bloody banner is raised!”</b>
</i><br /><br />This book is a perfect example why I think rating books with numbers (of stars or pine cones or whatever else you could think of) is needless and futile. <br />Is <i>Valour</i> the greatest book I have ever read? Hell no.<br />Is it a good one? Couldn’t say that either.<br />Then it’s a bad one? No, no, no.<br />Then what is?<br />It’s a decent enough book. <br />And if we’re going to be “strictly technical” <i>Valour’s</i> worth is of two stars.<br />It sure is better than <i>Malice</i> - that convoluted and predictable mess of a book. <br /><br />So two stars – that means I didn’t like it very much, right?<br />No, actually I enjoyed reading this book. And I can’t wait to continue with next one in the series.<br />Honestly, I couldn’t care less how big or small number of stars anyone gives to any book they read.<br />Daily I read dozen of reviews and I barely even notice how many stars reviewer gave to it.<br />(Because I’m already preoccupied with reading a review, obviously. :D)<br />And that’s only significant thing I’ll ever need to see if a person liked a book or not. Number or a star won’t cut it. <br />It wouldn’t explain, it wouldn’t suffice and it will never substitute your words. It’s never that simple.<br />That’s why I think rating books like we do is pointless.<br />And I see people longing for that half star… Yes, because in-between 4 or 5 a 4.5 star would be a decider. :D:D<br /><br />Now, back to actual review. :D <br /><i>Valour</i>, second book in “<i>The Faithful and the Fallen</i>” series is a better book than the first one - <i>Malice</i>. <br />Many problems that I had with the first book luckily stayed there. <br />Some didn’t bother me as much and to some I got used to and accepted them.<br /><br />- Who would think that problem with pacing could be so easily solved with just one sentence, here and there, beginning with: “<i>And a few/many days/nights months, moons and morrows after…</i>”<br />And just like that - I lost impression that characters are simply teleporting themselves throughout the map. Actually, this time it was so well done and organized that I didn’t even need a map to see where characters are nor where they are heading. <br />And probably that’s because another problem that I had stayed with the first book.<br /><br />- Abundance of characters and their POV chapters. There’s 120 chapters in this book. The biggest one probably not even 5 pages long. <br />And yet, confusion of “<i>who and what and where</i>” that bothered me in previous book wasn’t present in this one. Partially because more than half of the characters I already knew, but mostly because - again - John neatly organized “<i>who and what and where</i>” of his characters that he want’s from us in story to follow.<br /><br />And the problem that still persists, but the one that I got used to: <br />- Prose and predictability where this story goes. That’s all I’m going to say about that.<br /><br />Characters: some got under my skin. <br /><i>Cywen</i>. The main reason why I even continued reading this series, honestly. Perfect bigger sister and a really great character. <br /><i>Corban</i>. He was really a <i>Bright Star</i> of the first book. And he annoyed me throughout his “<i>Rand Al-Tor</i>” faze in <i>Valour</i>. “<i>I will not let Aes Sedai to control me!</i>” flashbacks were strong while reading his chapters.<br />But, he’s a good lad. Can’t wait to read more of him.<br />Also <i>Camlin</i> and <i>Gar</i>, now <i>Maquin</i> and <i>Fidele</i>.<br /><i>Veradis</i>… I’m excited to read more of him even though I already know where his story leads to. <br /><br />All in all, this was a really fun read of an average book. <br />There’s a great and innovative idea inside of John’s mind. And I can’t wait to read about next world he’ll create.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17879433320706899037" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
