<div id="review_2019543489" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2019543489" />
    <a title="Alagaesia.Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56671375-alagaesia-books"><img alt="Alagaesia.Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1490387179p2/56671375.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2019543489?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alagaesia.Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alagaesia.Books" href="/user/show/56671375-alagaesia-books">Alagaesia.Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780330545761" href="/book/show/23248251-valour">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Alagaesia.Books by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56671375-alagaesia-books?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2019543489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5130215425467308672">So in my review of Malice I already said that I found a new favourite series and now after finishing Valour I’m more certain about this than ever!<br/>Where Malice felt more like a long and well developing introduction Valour was like a great action packed journey through a world I got to know parts of in the first book with character you came to love. <br/>It had everything I loved about Malice and more. More amazing fighting scenes, more emotion, more character development; I just feel like being a part</span>
  <span id="freeText5130215425467308672" style="display:none">So in my review of Malice I already said that I found a new favourite series and now after finishing Valour I’m more certain about this than ever!<br />Where Malice felt more like a long and well developing introduction Valour was like a great action packed journey through a world I got to know parts of in the first book with character you came to love. <br />It had everything I loved about Malice and more. More amazing fighting scenes, more emotion, more character development; I just feel like being a part of this world more than ever.<br /><br />The story starts right where we left and puts on a fast pace since the very first page, with no indication of slowing down. This was mostly created by the various and sometimes rather short POVs. I was worried that it might be too much characters and too short chapters but in the end I see that there was nothing to worry about. The change in character, in POV, with every chapter is what makes this series so special because Gwynne I freaking good at this. Every chapter, every story line was interesting leaving me at the end of every one of it wanting to continue the story with this character. And by the time story lines crossed and characters met one another I often caught myself grinning like a total dork or gaping open mothed.<br />But though I loved literally every bit of this book there are two things I want to note that made me fell for it even more:<br />First: again the character development (and of cause the characters themself). There’s not much to say about this though. It was just amazingly writing, plausible and most of all relatable. I just love how Gwynne makes his characters evolve!<br />And second: <b>freakingly great written, strong female characters!! <br /></b><br />To explain this point I have to say that I’m a sucker for fantasy novels especially high fantasy. And well the fact is that there are only few books (that I know of) with strong, well-written and for me as a girl relatable female characters. So I have to thank Mr. Gwynne with all my heart for giving me female characters I can relate to.<br /><br />All in all I have to say that I love Valour and the Faithful and The Fallen! I’m happy I started reading this series and I can’t wait to continue it with reading Ruin!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5130215425467308672" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1756546385" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1756546385" />
    <a title="TS Chan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan"><img alt="TS Chan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543800303p2/30279227.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1756546385?book_show_action=true">Sep 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TS Chan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TS Chan" href="/user/show/30279227-ts-chan">TS Chan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/21324349-valour">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1756546385" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10673071199953802365"><b>Buddy Read with my awesome buddies at BB&B.</b><br/><br/>Well done, Mr Gwynne, well done! An absolutely worthy and breathtaking sequel that had me <b>completely and irrevocably invested</b> in the plot and the characters. When you start to take little breaks, breath heavily and notice your hands involuntarily making fists throughout the crucial battle scenes involving your favourite characters, you know are all-in. <br/><br/>My emotional investment in the main characters, even those without POVs (including the non-humans, ani</span>
  <span id="freeText10673071199953802365" style="display:none"><b>Buddy Read with my awesome buddies at BB&amp;B.</b><br /><br />Well done, Mr Gwynne, well done! An absolutely worthy and breathtaking sequel that had me <b>completely and irrevocably invested</b> in the plot and the characters. When you start to take little breaks, breath heavily and notice your hands involuntarily making fists throughout the crucial battle scenes involving your favourite characters, you know are all-in. <br /><br />My emotional investment in the main characters, even those without POVs (including the non-humans, animals, birds), amplified by the themes of friendship and loyalty, made this book positively engaging. While I'll not strictly classify this series in the grimdark vein, there are a lot of brutality and dark, disturbing and depressing scenes and moments throughout the narrative. Some of the action/fight scenes are violently portrayed and sometimes I wonder if I really should be reading this during my mealtimes.<br /><br />Thematically similar to classic fantasy with a prophecy and avatars of good and evil, the slight twist here is that Mr Evil Avatar was resoundingly deceived and honestly thought he was working towards the greater good. Along the way, he gained a number of allies and numbered amongst them are a few of the vilest creatures - and one good man who is a blind-sided loyal and true friend. It is going to be really interesting to see how this relationship plays out in the rest of the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10673071199953802365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1586906854" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1586906854" />
    <a title="Sam" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3300744-sam"><img alt="Sam" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1271108982p2/3300744.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1586906854?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sam" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sam" href="/user/show/3300744-sam">Sam</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780316399746" href="/book/show/18513718-valor">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3300744-sam?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3300744-sam?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1586906854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13437407240104564949">This. Book. I literally just finished it and it’s a very powerful ending. SO much finally comes together. It will basically leave you breathless. 5 star ending. 3 star beginning. I’m going to leave my rating at 4 stars for now. <br/><br/>Valor picks up right where Malice left off, but there was just something keeping me from being totally invested in the book in the beginning. The action slowed back down a bit from Malice which might be part of it, but I feel like there’s some weird personal issue of mine</span>
  <span id="freeText13437407240104564949" style="display:none">This. Book. I literally just finished it and it’s a very powerful ending. SO much finally comes together. It will basically leave you breathless. 5 star ending. 3 star beginning. I’m going to leave my rating at 4 stars for now. <br /><br />Valor picks up right where Malice left off, but there was just something keeping me from being totally invested in the book in the beginning. The action slowed back down a bit from Malice which might be part of it, but I feel like there’s some weird personal issue of mine with the writing style or something. I haven’t really been able to pin down what it is yet. The best I can tell is that the dialogue feels a bit stilted. I definitely think it’s improved from the first book, but every once in a while, the issue pops back up and I feel like something keeps the conversations between characters from flowing. I still keep reading, but I just don’t feel completely immersed until the action really picks up.<br /><br />The characters are the stars of the show though. A good character-driven book can overcome a lot. I’m impressed given the giant cast of characters (POV or not) there are that I end up liking so many of them. A lot of the side characters are developed with great personalities: Halion, Dath, Farrell, Alcyon, Rath, Conall, Orgull, Marrock, Brina. They feel different although there is a slight trend to the goods are good and bads are bad. I thought Malice felt a little more morally gray or at least a little more divided in their decisions. It’s not a bad thing persay, just a bit of a shift which might be because most of the characters have picked their sides now. This book is fairly grimdark and I typically think of grimdark characters as being quite morally gray. It’s interesting to read one where I feel characters are really striving to do good/be good even if they keep getting the shaft.<br /><br />I don’t think there was a POV I didn’t like in this book. Maquin’s story easily trumps Kastell although I do wish the feud with Jael was a little more fleshed out. Yes Jael is a bad guy, but I’ve never felt anything personal with the feud. I can understand the motivations, but I just wish I felt them. I wish there had been more Veradis as well. He was a great character in the first book and I thought he felt shuffled to the background in Valor. Lots of look menacing and shield-wall. Plus I would have loved a closer look at Nathair. I still have trouble believing he’s just completely that stupid. <br /><br />I loved catching up with all my favorites from Malice. Corban, Cywen, Camlin (so many C’s!). Definitely learning not to get too attached to any side-characters though. =/ RIP. Maybe not as much development in the characters as Malice but also not as much time passes in Valor. There’s at least enough to make me happy for now.<br /><br />I loved the addition of Coralen and Fidele. Definitely great to have more women POVs. Although Fidele… =(<br /><br />I thought the plot advanced nicely for a second book. The beginning was a large chunk of maneuvering people to places but I thought that smoothed out nicely towards the end where plot things happened while maneuvering. I’m excited to hopefully get more of the mythology/God-war background in the next book. I feel like all the key players/pieces have been introduced so I can’t wait to see what starts happening with them. <br /><br />A couple of nitpicky things: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I’m a little sick of the shield wall. I get the German tribes/Roman legion vibe but the 1000 men vs 10000 men in an open field? =/ The shield wall was good, but not unbeatable. Also why did Fech completely glob on to Edana and not fly back to Nemain? He knew Uthas was a traitor and really mourns Nemain at the end. Even if he was information gathering, he still hung out with Corban some instead of delivering the message and flying straight to Nemain.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><i>They must be stopped.</i> That ending though. Super strong. Just a wash of emotion. I really hope the momentum of Valor carries better into Ruin than Malice did into Valor.<br /><br />Definitely recommend Valor and the series overall. It’s not reinventing fantasy but it’s everything I love about fantasy done well. Once the story and the characters sinks their hooks into you, the pages will fly by. I can’t wait to start Book 3 and I’ve already ordered Book 4.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13437407240104564949" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VE3lxCRDhURLUwLG85eOTmCzpZy2zZUm/Yogs5Lxu1Vxwp1uDReAtao1ef2fwPbmneZ0HVzGnMot8jMUTu1m5g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GjvUR6fVpwDKnxq6Opj67AQNdWw8znW873YPTB19cB4/tKztjoGi8Sv5YYFWz4JE+Vik7dbFfFA/DhzrwWGtrQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13764630568222040913">Malice is my debut novel. Goldsboro Books of London, specialists in signed first-editions, have made Malice their 'Book of the Month' for December 2012.<br/><br/>I was born in Singapore while my dad was stationed there in the RAF. Up until he retired that meant a lot of traveling around, generally a move every three years or so.<br/><br/>I live with my wife and four wonderful (and demanding) children in East Sussex. </span>
  <span id="freeText13764630568222040913" style="display:none">Malice is my debut novel. Goldsboro Books of London, specialists in signed first-editions, have made Malice their 'Book of the Month' for December 2012.<br /><br />I was born in Singapore while my dad was stationed there in the RAF. Up until he retired that meant a lot of traveling around, generally a move every three years or so.<br /><br />I live with my wife and four wonderful (and demanding) children in East Sussex. Also three dogs, two of which will chew anything that stands still. I have had many strange and wonderful jobs, including packing soap in a soap factory, waitering in a french restaurant in Canada, playing double bass in a rock n roll band, and lecturing at Brighton University.<br /><br />I stepped out of university work due to my daughter’s disability, so now I split my time caring for her and working from home - I work with my wife rejuvenating vintage furniture, which means fixing, lifting, carrying, painting and generally doing what my wife tells me to do...<br /><br />And somehow during this time I started writing. I’ve always told my children stories at bed-time, and they pestered long and hard for me to write some of it down. At the same time I felt that my brain was switching off a little - vintage furniture is my wife’s passion, whereas my passions are geekier!<br /><br />That’s how The Banished Lands and Malice began, though along the way it became more than just a hobby. I’m still in shock that it is actually a real book, rather than just pages on my desk. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13764630568222040913" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
